<div id="review_1586695595" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1586695595" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6217162-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430955688p2/6217162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1586695595?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/6217162-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6217162-donna?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6217162-donna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6217162-donna?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6217162-donna?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1586695595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13127816229836012366">"My name is Brás de Oliva Domingos, and I'm a dreamer...What my dreams really show me is what my life can be once I open my eyes...My dreams tell me who I am."<br/><br/>Image from <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345768i/700360.jpg'>http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo...</a>.<br/><br/>This Eisner award winning graphic novel was my latest vehicle used to explore this genre, and it took me on quite a trip. At first, I wasn't sure what was happening in the story or where it would lead, which was nothing new for me. I'm often clueless at the start of a book and can only ho</span>
  <span id="freeText13127816229836012366" style="display:none">"My name is Brás de Oliva Domingos, and I'm a dreamer...What my dreams really show me is what my life can be once I open my eyes...My dreams tell me who I am."<br /><br />Image from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345768i/700360.jpg">http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo...</a>.<br /><br />This Eisner award winning graphic novel was my latest vehicle used to explore this genre, and it took me on quite a trip. At first, I wasn't sure what was happening in the story or where it would lead, which was nothing new for me. I'm often clueless at the start of a book and can only hope all will become clear by the end. I've learned to suppress my discomfort at not having all the answers I'd like, until a good portion of the book is underway. I tell myself this is good for me, trusting in an author, as long as the author doesn't let me down. And I'm happy to say, the authors of this book, who also drew the amazing illustrations, came through for me, creating a life affirming story about the inevitability of death. <br /><br />Fábio Moon and Gabriel Bá, the creators of this novel, which was originally published as a ten part comics series, are twin brothers from Brazil, where this story takes place. Their book is steeped in Latin American culture, blending a highly realistic and emotional story with magical realism, a challenging combination that worked. The main character, Brás, is a writer who at the age of 32, when we first meet him, works on a newspaper composing obituaries instead of covering the news breaking stories he dreamed of, or writing the important novel he believes he has inside him. His father, a famous writer, is a national treasure and has some very big shoes for Brás to fill. Brás broods about this and what direction his life has taken him in, which is away from his dreams. As he says to his best friend, "I wanted to write about life, Jorge, and look at me now...all I write about is death."<br /><br />Image from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://hellocomic.com/img/magazines/daytripper/daytripper-01/daytripper_01_08.jpg">http://hellocomic.com/img/magazines/d...</a>.<br /><br />How Brás came to this frustrating point in his life and where he will go from there unfolds in this novel which is divided into chapters showing Brás at different stages in his life that end abruptly just as he comes to a turning point. And this is where the novel gets tricky as it leaps forward and backward in time, in a nonlinear fashion, giving the reader glimpses of Brás' struggles at each key age, where a decision of his defines his fate which seems to be the same no matter what action he takes. So what's the point of life when it will always end the same way--in death? This is what Brás will discover over a lifetime. <br /><br /><br />Image from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://rouamat.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/daytripper_2.jpg">http://rouamat.com/wp-content/uploads...</a>.<br /><br />Image from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://comicsbulletin.com/main/sites/default/files/full/images/daytripper/daytrripper-magnett1.jpg">http://comicsbulletin.com/main/sites/...</a>.<br /><br />Image from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://comicsalliance.com/files/2011/02/daytrip03.jpg">http://comicsalliance.com/files/2011/...</a>.<br /><br />Image from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://static.comicvine.com/uploads/original/4/48443/1228419-daytripper_4_27.jpg">http://static.comicvine.com/uploads/o...</a>.<br /><br />Image from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://cdn.journalism.cuny.edu/blogs.dir/226/files/2011/01/screen-shot-2011-01-12-at-11-52-36-pm.png">http://cdn.journalism.cuny.edu/blogs....</a>.<br /><br /><br />Did I mention this graphic novel is deep? Did I remember to tell you how the illustrations are rich in detail that express emotion while the captions ask the big questions about life? Did I forget to say that the relationships between the characters are well defined as are the characters themselves, as much as you could hope for in any satisfying novel? Well, if I did forget, I've mentioned it now. And darn if I didn't end up crying at the end of this book which really took me by surprise. That's how affecting it was when I was only expecting to enjoy some cool illustrations in what seemed like a concept book. But this book is about family and a person's place in it, as well as a person's place in the world and in his dreams. Brás realizes, "As the seed of his family tree started to grow and make sense in his mind, the seasons were changing inside of him." And "Home is not a physical place at all but a group of elements like the people you live with--a feeling, a state of mind...He feels safer just knowing that even if he's away, there is a home waiting for him to return."<br /><br />So this book is about a lot of things, though mainly dreams, which everyone has, as well as the things that stop us from making them into reality--the excuses...the need to hide from possible failure. But it's really about letting go of the dreams and living life which may not measure up to the dreams, but the dreams don't need to die because of it when life takes that new direction. <br /><br />"Take a deep breath, open your eyes <br />and close the book." </span>
  <a data-text-id="13127816229836012366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14365196253929033231">I never picked up this book and bought it because of the cover art and the description; for some reason, it seemed like it wouldn't interest me. However, a good friend gave it to me to read, and has consistently recommended good books to me, so I gave it a chance, and I am so glad that I did. The art was incredibly gorgeous, and the story was touching--honestly, this is the first graphic novel that ever made me tear up. It's rare for me these days to find a book that I wish hadn't ended when I f</span>
  <span id="freeText14365196253929033231" style="display:none">I never picked up this book and bought it because of the cover art and the description; for some reason, it seemed like it wouldn't interest me. However, a good friend gave it to me to read, and has consistently recommended good books to me, so I gave it a chance, and I am so glad that I did. The art was incredibly gorgeous, and the story was touching--honestly, this is the first graphic novel that ever made me tear up. It's rare for me these days to find a book that I wish hadn't ended when I finally read the last page, close it and put it down for good, but this is certainly one of them. If you like beautiful art, exploration of the intricacies of life, and excellent story-telling abilities, this book is absolutely for you.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2891053762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2891053762" />
    <a title="Diana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89242656-diana"><img alt="Diana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565726515p2/89242656.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2891053762?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana" href="/user/show/89242656-diana">Diana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89242656-diana?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2891053762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12465859635376167379">Daytripper [2010/11] – ★★★★★<br/><br/>Fábio Moon and Gabriel Bá are twin brothers from Brazil who are the creators of Daytripper, an ambitious comic book about Bras de Oliva Domingos, an obituaries’ writer living in Sao Paulo. We follow and experience his life in a non-chronological order and witness everything from Bras’s “unusual” birth, his first kiss, his major break-up, his career change, to the birth of his child and the death of his parent. Bras learns important life-lessons along the way, and it i</span>
  <span id="freeText12465859635376167379" style="display:none">Daytripper [2010/11] – ★★★★★<br /><br />Fábio Moon and Gabriel Bá are twin brothers from Brazil who are the creators of Daytripper, an ambitious comic book about Bras de Oliva Domingos, an obituaries’ writer living in Sao Paulo. We follow and experience his life in a non-chronological order and witness everything from Bras’s “unusual” birth, his first kiss, his major break-up, his career change, to the birth of his child and the death of his parent. Bras learns important life-lessons along the way, and it is his relationships with other people that come to define him and his most memorable life moments. Daytripper may be dealing with very uncomfortable issues of life and death, but this beautiful comic book is also eye-opening, inspirational and moving. Gabriel Bá and Fábio Moon invite you to step into their colourful, slightly transcendental world of one’s memorable life moments, into the world of “what ifs”, ups and downs, hopes and despairs. Their message is clear: we have one shot at this thing called life and should prioritise the most important things in it, including the people we cherish and the relationships we hold dear. Daytripper is simply an exhilarating journey to uncover the mysteries of life and death. <br /><br />The comic book starts with Bras as a thirty-two year old obituaries’ writer who is disillusioned about his career of a book writer. His best friend Jorge tries to cheer him up as Bras prepares to attend one of his father’s big events. He does not make it…he is killed on his way there. Moon and Bá capture and hold their readers’ attention with the repeated deaths of their hero Bras, a guy we start to sympathise with a lot as the story moves forwards…and backwards (each chapter ends with a tragedy). At another point, Bras is a carefree twenty-one year old, enjoying his vacation in El Salvador with his best friend Jorge. There, he meets beautiful Olinda. Jorge and Olinda, as well as Bras’s parents, almost act as spiritual companions/guides in Bras’s life journey, teaching him valuable life lessons – directly or indirectly. Bras’s relationship with Jorge is particularly moving. Jorge is the man who teaches Bras how to relax and enjoy each moment in life – he shows him the fun side of life. Bras, in turn, keeps wild Jorge, a photographer, grounded.<br /><br />The theme of life and death, as well as the meaning of life, is at the very centre of Daytripper. The authors want their readers to ask such questions as – “what is the most important thing in our lives?” and “If something bad happens tomorrow, have we lived true to ourselves and to those dear to us?”. These are not the questions one will ask on a daily basis or even want to ask oneself, but Moon and Bá present their “thesis” in such an enjoyable and thought-provoking format, one will ponder about these questions when reading the comic book and be happy to do so. We are shown Bras at various stages of his life – and most of them end abruptly. The point is clear: do not wait for an opportunity, create it and take it (tomorrow may not come). Bras learns something profound at each period of his life and it is only by living through his experiences he is able to know – there is no shortcut to the answers.<br /><br />When Bras has to deal with sorrow and grief in his life, we are taken on this ride too. Meetings and partings are all part and parcel of a thing called life, just as losses, loneliness and new beginnings are. The courage is to make those new beginnings, the story says. By writing about death and the lives of others, Bras actually gains a new perspective on life and its meaning, and, as he becomes more reflective, so do we as we read his story. Bras battles his own inner demons when he knows at some point that his career of a writer is going nowhere – “he knew he has been running away from his dreams….because he was afraid of failing” [Fábio Moon and Gabriel Bá, 2011: 210] – and even though the readers may be far from creative pursuits, Bras’s story somehow feels very relatable and personal. The joys of friendship, romantic love and parenthood – they all sit there alongside the chance of a heart-break, uncertainty and depression, but this insightful comic book has many other observations to make, including on the true nature of people: “Everybody has to work, right?….these people in here who have to do something to get by…But, that doesn’t tell you who these people truly are” [Fábio Moon and Gabriel Bá, 2011: 47], explains Olinda passionately to Bras at a street market. The nearness of death in the story also gives a new perspective on life, and there are still surprises when finally facing the expected and the inevitable – it is when death is so close that life (and its meaning) is suddenly so clear and simple. Near the end of the story, Bras’s life journey becomes dream-like, possibly because he is now closer than ever to uncover the mysteries of life.<br /><br />The comic book is not all about philosophical considerations and transcendental experiences, however – there is much humour and dramatic moments which make for a roller-coaster of a reading ride, especially when coupled with chaotic time sequences and memory “flashes”. Some moments are so dramatic as to be laughable, but the main talent of the brothers still lies in capturing the nuances and “still” moments, things left unsaid or silences that speak louder than words. In this sense, some pictures in this graphic novel are really “worth a thousand words”. The comic’s colours (red to signify danger; bluish colours to signify sadness; and bright colours to signify carefree childhood, for example) and transport depiction (a boat, a train), to stand for the passage of time, are other clever devices to make the story more impactful.<br /><br />Fábio Moon and Gabriel Bá’s beautifully-illustrated comic book is something very special: it presents timeless themes in an entertaining format, and makes one wonder and ponder about the meaning of life and things that make it all worthwhile. Daytripper may not be a comfortable ride, but it is a necessary one for everyone – so significant and deep its messages are. Like a good cup of coffee the twin creators love so much, Daytripper is sometimes "bitter", sometimes "sweet", but it still guarantees to give you "a boost" – a boost you will not forget any time soon and will want to come back to again and again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12465859635376167379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16884623690666747819">Daytripper moved me so much, I was not moved at all, I was reminded. I was reminded how magical the smell of a hand-rolled cohiba, the bitter taste of cachaca, and a dimly lit bar makes my brain feel so loose and heavenly inside my head. A poignant story, with illustrations so fluid and seamless they fill the tiny spaces between thoughts to make the whole experience just, BEAUTIFUL. <br/><br/>I was left with the feeling of hanging on, ever so carefully, balanced safely, precisely, but defiantly on the edg</span>
  <span id="freeText16884623690666747819" style="display:none">Daytripper moved me so much, I was not moved at all, I was reminded. I was reminded how magical the smell of a hand-rolled cohiba, the bitter taste of cachaca, and a dimly lit bar makes my brain feel so loose and heavenly inside my head. A poignant story, with illustrations so fluid and seamless they fill the tiny spaces between thoughts to make the whole experience just, BEAUTIFUL. <br /><br />I was left with the feeling of hanging on, ever so carefully, balanced safely, precisely, but defiantly on the edge, where that ONE careless action of “wait ...wait, I’m sure I left my self around here somewhere?” represents a tiny, silent, still, feeling that changes your entire life. A powerful feeling that you will never forget, but also a devastating knowledge that you will never remember every beautiful, insignificant, and enormously heartbreaking detail. Intense and simple. Such is life. <br /><br />If Sylvain Chomet (Les Triplettes de Belleville) made this into a movie, it would rescue millions of people from a shallow grave. It’s one of those things that comes along in the midst of the intense and immediate need to make it all come undone for reasons only you can imagine, that tiny thing that makes everything spill out, everything, everywhere, tumbling toward where ever AWAY is at that moment of awe-full discovery, at the ending of something. That thing that gives hope. <br /><br />GIVES. <br /><br />HOPE. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16884623690666747819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5014720818365624460">Elegant, both in words and drawing. This story examines the value of a life, told through time bending the date of death of a newspaper obituary writer. Emotional on many levels, the piece that strikes me the hardest is how obituaries are for the living, as if we put a stationery seal on the envelope at the end of a loved one's life. <br/><br/>Last summer, someone I once loved very much died. Here is his obituary:<br/><br/>"*** was born on April 5, 1970 and passed away on Saturday, July 2, 2011.<br/>*** was a resident o</span>
  <span id="freeText5014720818365624460" style="display:none">Elegant, both in words and drawing. This story examines the value of a life, told through time bending the date of death of a newspaper obituary writer. Emotional on many levels, the piece that strikes me the hardest is how obituaries are for the living, as if we put a stationery seal on the envelope at the end of a loved one's life. <br /><br />Last summer, someone I once loved very much died. Here is his obituary:<br /><br />"*** was born on April 5, 1970 and passed away on Saturday, July 2, 2011.<br />*** was a resident of San Francisco, California."<br /><br />What does that mean? I want a nice little bow. I want to know if he had children? Did he like his work? Did he find beauty in each day? Did he suffer, or pass peacefully at home surrounded by friends? What where his joys and personal demons? <br /><br />Did he ever think of me? <br /><br />Bá and Moon know you can't summarize a person's life in a tiny newspaper column, and they show us in each frame, through word and color and nuance, capturing the emotion of the life (and sometimes the detachment from emotion,) and reminding us that, no matter how gracefully written, you cannot distill the essence of living into a paragraph or two starting: "He was..."<br /><br />But it helps the living. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5014720818365624460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_514085197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/514085197" />
    <a title="Bruce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/897874-bruce"><img alt="Bruce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1202929351p2/897874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/514085197?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bruce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bruce" href="/user/show/897874-bruce">Bruce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/897874-bruce?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/897874-bruce?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer514085197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18025339920105032259"><i>"I gotta tell you… I really liked today's obits. They're different, somehow. Deeper. You're really pouring your heart into them."<br/><br/>"It's all crap. I'm a fraud." (p. 145)<br/><br/>"… nothing in my life is <b>extraordinary</b>. Nothing in my life really <b>matters</b>."( p. 149)</i><br/><br/>There in the words of its characters lies my critique of this well-intentioned graphic novel. <br/><br/>This is a book of lofty ambition; the authors intending to point up the fragile beauty evoked through milestone, quotidian days in the life of an obituary </span>
  <span id="freeText18025339920105032259" style="display:none"><i>"I gotta tell you… I really liked today's obits. They're different, somehow. Deeper. You're really pouring your heart into them."<br /><br />"It's all crap. I'm a fraud." (p. 145)<br /><br />"… nothing in my life is <b>extraordinary</b>. Nothing in my life really <b>matters</b>."( p. 149)</i><br /><br />There in the words of its characters lies my critique of this well-intentioned graphic novel. <br /><br />This is a book of lofty ambition; the authors intending to point up the fragile beauty evoked through milestone, quotidian days in the life of an obituary writer/aspiring author at 11, 28, 32, 41, etc. Their conceit is to close the events of each chapter day with the writer's death and likely obituary. One could seek to find a literal explanation for this. You might have it that the deaths are but the protagonist's morbid fantasies. An alternative possibility could be that our hero is lucky enough to have the multiple lives of a cat but the misfortune to need them. The authors retconned a third rationale that justifies the conceit without really resolving the narrative discontinuities. Given that <u>Daytripper</u> is readily understood to be a work of fiction, I'm not sure that any explanation was necessary.<br /> <br />Suffice it to say that it's a tough conceit to carry off, and it didn't work for me. <br /><br />Not that I am likely to persuade anyone to undertake a revised edition, but now that I've seen the storyboard -- and I deride the otherwise impeccable brushwork thus for the cheap resort to crude penmanship that falls between pp. 208-219; albeit done with narrative purpose, it was still jarringly bad to view -- here are my two big notes. First, giving each chapter full closure robs the book as a whole of both narrative arc and continuity. If you can shuffle the chapter order without meaningfully impacting the theme or story as you can here, then your work as an author is not truly done. Ever read a book that was easy to put down? Three chapters in and I'm revving up to start skimming. Yikes.<br /><br />The other problem lurking in the conceit is more profound, in that it led to me ceasing to care about the characters in the book. Death is the ultimate consequence. There are no higher stakes than those of an existential conflict. The linear suspense this generates can be deployed as a narrative engine forward (Will the hero survive? Does the hero deserve to live?) or in flashback. (Why did the hero die? What significance did the hero's death have?) However, invoking a single-beat rhythm of chapter-ending caesurae through a sequence of unrelated, arbitrary endings, removes conflict and unpredictability. A tiresome pattern quickly emerges such that either each demise or the circumstances preceding them cease to matter. With no turning of the screw, no stakes or consequences, why care? Though I read this all the way through, my lack of simpatico for the cast and plot killed off any chance for me to feel the impact the authors presumably intended.<br /><br />Experience is subjective of course, and your results will vary. For that reason I strongly recommend you consider GR Seth Hahne's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148646758" rel="nofollow noopener">rave review</a> and draw your own conclusion about whether or not to seek this out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18025339920105032259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_298332872" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/298332872" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/298332872?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer298332872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9275547004766226662">It's hard for me to write a review about a book like Daytripper. It's too well-written. The art is too beautiful. The characters are too real. The story is too moving and life affirming. I can't write about Daytripper. It's too wonderful, too close to perfect. All I can say is how grateful I am that I had the chance to read it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HtO2lNloFyB3DLCjZTklzaszBmcXnyr0o4/5UUnVYwxKPpBKC5FZXx31yNj4Y3pHzSvZwqGMV4gcuCh/PDXFYQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0k5Ia6SecjxO6YKVvt2qxvpTqcYUe3iKcNU+69nY/imGo261dmc8QyQQ+u4jh/VMnEt2Y6JoBfbP4u/FrDhYRA==')})
  }

What turns two brothers from an unstoppable team into a pair of bitterly estranged loners? How does the simple-hearted care of one middle-aged nurse reveal the scars of an entire community, and can anything heal the wounds caused by a century of deception?\n\nAward-winning cartoonist Jeff Lemire pays tribute to his roots with Essex County, an award-winning trilogy of graphic novels set in an imaginary version of his hometown, the eccentric farming community of Essex County, Ontario, Canada. In Essex County, Lemire crafts an intimate study of one community through the years, and a tender meditation on family, memory, grief, secrets, and reconciliation. Now, in this provocative graphic novel, Vaughan examines life on the streets of war-torn Iraq. In the spring of 2003, a pride of lions escaped from the Baghdad zoo during an American bombing raid. Lost and confused, hungry but finally free, the four lions roamed the decimated streets of Baghdad in a desperate struggle for their lives.
